<p><i><b>...Baby One More Time</b></i> is the debut <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Studio_album" title="Studio album">studio album</a> by American recording artist <a href="/wiki/Britney_Spears" title="Britney Spears">Britney Spears</a>. It was released on January 12, 1999, by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/JIVE_Records" title="JIVE Records">JIVE Records</a>. In June 1997, while Spears negotiated with manager <a href="/wiki/Lou_Pearlman" title="Lou Pearlman">Lou Pearlman</a> to join female pop group <a href="/wiki/Innosense" title="Innosense">Innosense</a>, her mother asked family friend and entertainment lawyer <a href="/wiki/Larry_Rudolph" title="Larry Rudolph">Larry Rudolph</a> for his opinion and submitted a tape of Spears singing over a <a href="/wiki/Whitney_Houston" title="Whitney Houston">Whitney Houston</a> <a href="/wiki/Karaoke" title="Karaoke">karaoke</a> song. Rudolph decided to pitch her to record labels, sending them a demo tape with an unused song from <a href="/wiki/Toni_Braxton" title="Toni Braxton">Toni Braxton</a>. JIVE was interested and appointed the singer to work with producer Eric Foster White. After hearing the recorded material, JIVE signed Spears to a multi-album deal.</p>
<p>Spears traveled to Sweden to work with producers <a href="/wiki/Max_Martin" title="Max Martin">Max Martin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Denniz_Pop" title="Denniz Pop">Denniz Pop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rami_Yacoub" title="Rami Yacoub">Rami Yacoub</a>, among others. Martin showed Spears and her management a track titled "Hit Me Baby One More Time", which was originally written for American R&amp;B group <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TLC_(band)" title="TLC (band)">TLC</a>; however, they rejected the track. Spears later claimed that she felt excited when she heard it and knew it was going to be a hit record. By June 1998, the album had been finished.</p>
<p>Critics gave the album mixed reviews, describing the singer as a <a href="/wiki/Madonna_(entertainer)" title="Madonna (entertainer)">Madonna</a> next door, considering it silly and premature. The album was successful on the charts, reaching the top five in several countries, while reaching number one in Canada and the United States. It also received several certifications around the world, including a <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certification" title="RIAA certification">fourteen-times platinum</a> certification by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> (RIAA), for shipments of over 14 million units in the country. <i>...Baby One More Time</i> is Spears' most successful album, selling over 30 million copies worldwide, making it one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_albums" title="List of best-selling albums">best-selling albums of all time</a> and the best-selling album by a teenage solo artist.</p>
<p>Five singles came from the album. "...Baby One More Time" became a worldwide success and one of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_singles_worldwide" title="List of best-selling singles worldwide">best-selling singles of all time</a>, at over ten million copies. The album was promoted with appearances on live television, and also by the <a href="/wiki/...Baby_One_More_Time_Tour" title="...Baby One More Time Tour">...Baby One More Time Tour</a> in 1999, with a second leg titled <a href="/wiki/...Baby_One_More_Time_Tour" title="...Baby One More Time Tour">Crazy 2k Tour</a> in 2000. Spears claimed she wasn't able to explore her vocal ability on the album. This album set Spears' international <a href="/wiki/Pop_icon" title="Pop icon">pop culture icon</a> image and launched her career. The album earned Spears <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grammy" title="Grammy">Grammy</a> nominations for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Best_New_Artist" title="Best New Artist">Best New Artist</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Best_Female_Pop_Vocal_Performance" title="Best Female Pop Vocal Performance">Best Female Pop Vocal Performance</a> for "...Baby One More Time."</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background_and_development">Background and development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=...Baby_One_More_Time_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background and development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: left; clear: left; margin: 0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0; width:30%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"I had been in studio for about six months listening and recording material, but I hadn't really heard a hit yet. When I started working with Max Martin in Sweden, he played the demo for 'Baby One More Time' for me, and I knew from the start it one was of those songs you want to hear again and again. It just felt really right. I went into the studio and did my own thing with it, trying to give it a little more attitude than the demo. In 10 days, I never even saw Sweden. We were so busy."</p>
</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: left;">—Spears talking to Chuck Taylor of <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup></cite></div>
<p>In June 1997, Spears was in talks with manager <a href="/wiki/Lou_Pearlman" title="Lou Pearlman">Lou Pearlman</a> to join female pop group Innosense. Lynne asked family friend and entertainment lawyer Larry Rudolph for his opinion and submitted a tape of Spears singing over a Whitney Houston karaoke song along with some pictures. Rudolph decided to pitch her to record labels, which required a professional <a href="/wiki/Demo_(music)" title="Demo (music)">demo</a>. He sent Spears an unused song from Toni Braxton; she rehearsed for a week and recorded in a studio with a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Audio_engineering" title="Audio engineering">sound engineer</a>. Spears traveled to New York with the demo and met executives from four labels, returning to Kentwood the same day. Three rejected her, arguing audiences wanted pop bands such as the <a href="/wiki/Backstreet_Boys" title="Backstreet Boys">Backstreet Boys</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Spice_Girls" title="Spice Girls">Spice Girls</a>, and "there wasn't going to be another Madonna, another <a href="/wiki/Debbie_Gibson" title="Debbie Gibson">Debbie Gibson</a> or another <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tiffany_(American_singer)" title="Tiffany (American singer)">Tiffany</a>." Two weeks later, executives from JIVE Records returned calls to Rudolph.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hughes145_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-hughes145-2">[2]</a></sup> Senior vice president of <a href="/wiki/Artists_and_repertoire" title="Artists and repertoire">A&amp;R</a> Jeff Fenster stated, "It's very rare to hear someone that age who can deliver emotional content and commercial appeal. [...] For any artist, the motivation—the 'eye of the tiger'— is extremely important. And Britney had that."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rs1_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-rs1-3">[3]</a></sup> They appointed her to work with producer Eric Foster White for a month, who reportedly shaped her voice from "lower and less poppy" delivery to "distinctively, unmistakably Britney."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hughes_2005_147_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hughes_2005_147-4">[4]</a></sup> Spears recorded ten songs with White, including "Autumn Goodbye", "E-Mail My Heart", "From the Bottom of My Broken Heart", "I'm So Curious", "I Will Still Love You", "Luv The Hurt Away", "Soda Pop", "Thinkin' About You", and "You Got It All".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-liner_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-liner-5">[5]</a></sup> The singer also recorded a cover of <a href="/wiki/Sonny_%26_Cher" title="Sonny &amp; Cher">Sonny &amp; Cher</a>'s 1967 single "<a href="/wiki/The_Beat_Goes_On_(Sonny_%26_Cher_song)" title="The Beat Goes On (Sonny &amp; Cher song)">The Beat Goes On</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-liner_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-liner-5">[5]</a></sup> White was responsible for the vocal recording and song production, while additional production was done by English electronic music group <a href="/wiki/All_Seeing_I" title="All Seeing I">All Seeing I</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-liner_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-liner-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>After hearing the material, president <a href="/wiki/Clive_Calder" title="Clive Calder">Clive Calder</a> ordered a full album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hughes_2005_147_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hughes_2005_147-4">[4]</a></sup> Spears flew to <a href="/wiki/Cheiron_Studios" title="Cheiron Studios">Cheiron Studios</a> in <a href="/wiki/Stockholm" title="Stockholm">Stockholm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>, where half of the album was recorded from March to April 1998, with producers Max Martin, Denniz Pop and Rami Yacoub, among others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rs1_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-rs1-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsintw_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-rsintw-6">[6]</a></sup> Martin showed Spears and her management a track titled "Hit Me Baby One More Time", which was originally written for American <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/R%26B" title="R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a> group <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TLC_(band)" title="TLC (band)">TLC</a>; however, they rejected it. Spears later claimed that she felt excited when she heard it and knew it was going to be a hit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-especial_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-especial-7">[7]</a></sup> "We at JIVE said, 'This is a fuckin' smash'," revealed the label's A&amp;R executive, Steven Lunt;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> however, other executives were concerned that the line "Hit Me" would condone <a href="/wiki/Domestic_violence" title="Domestic violence">domestic violence</a>, and later revised it to "...Baby One More Time".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-especial_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-especial-7">[7]</a></sup> The singer revealed that she "didn't do well at all the first day in the studio [recording the song], I was just too nervous. So I went out that night and had some fun. The next day I was completely relaxed and nailed it. You gotta be relaxed singing '... Baby One More Time'."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blender_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-blender-9">[9]</a></sup> By June 1998, the album was done,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> and Spears embarked on a promotional tour sponsored by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/L%27Oreal" title="L'Oreal">L'Oreal</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blandford28_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-blandford28-11">[11]</a></sup> <i>...Baby One More Time</i> was released as Spears' debut album on January 12, 1999.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Composition">Composition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=...Baby_One_More_Time_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Composition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Spears originally envisioned "<a href="/wiki/Sheryl_Crow" title="Sheryl Crow">Sheryl Crow</a> music, but younger more adult contemporary", but felt all right with her label's producers, since "It made more sense to go pop, because I can dance to it—it's more me."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rs1_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-rs1-3">[3]</a></sup> The album opens with the first single "<a href="/wiki/...Baby_One_More_Time_(song)" title="...Baby One More Time (song)">...Baby One More Time</a>", a <a href="/wiki/Teen_pop" title="Teen pop">teen pop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dance-pop" title="Dance-pop">dance-pop</a> song that begins with a three-note <a href="/wiki/Motif_(music)" title="Motif (music)">motif</a> in the bass range of the <a href="/wiki/Piano" title="Piano">piano</a>. The opening was compared to many other songs, such as "<a href="/wiki/We_Will_Rock_You" title="We Will Rock You">We Will Rock You</a>" (1977), "<a href="/wiki/Start_Me_Up" title="Start Me Up">Start Me Up</a>" (1981) and the theme song of the film <i><a href="/wiki/Jaws_(film)" title="Jaws (film)">Jaws</a></i> due to the fact the track "makes its presence known in exactly one second".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blender_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-blender-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> According to magazine <i><a href="/wiki/Blender_(magazine)" title="Blender (magazine)">Blender</a></i>, "...Baby One More Time" is composed by "<a href="/wiki/Wah-wah_(music)" title="Wah-wah (music)">wah-wah</a> guitar lines and <a href="/wiki/Electrocardiography" title="Electrocardiography">EKG</a>-machine bass-slaps".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blender_9-2"><a href="#cite_note-blender-9">[9]</a></sup> Claudia Mitchell and Jacqueline Reid-Walsh, authors of <i>Girl Culture: Studying girl culture : a readers' guide</i> (2008), observed that the lyrics of the song "gesture toward [Spears] longing for the return of an ex-boyfriend."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> The next song and third single, "<a href="/wiki/(You_Drive_Me)_Crazy" title="(You Drive Me) Crazy">(You Drive Me) Crazy</a>" runs through a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Down-tempo" title="Down-tempo">moderately slow</a> <a href="/wiki/Dance_music" title="Dance music">dance</a> <a href="/wiki/Beat_(music)" title="Beat (music)">beat</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> and has a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/R%26B" title="R&amp;B">rhythm and blues</a> <a href="/wiki/Melody" title="Melody">melody</a> mixed with edgy synthesized instrumentals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> The third track and second single "<a href="/wiki/Sometimes_(Britney_Spears_song)" title="Sometimes (Britney Spears song)">Sometimes</a>" is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ballad_(music)" title="Ballad (music)">ballad</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> that Spears begins with "You tell me you're in love with me/That you can't take your pretty eyes away from me/It's not that I don't wanna stay/But every time you come too close I move away".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Thomas_Erlewine" title="Stephen Thomas Erlewine">Stephen Thomas Erlewine</a> of <a href="/wiki/AllMusic" title="AllMusic">AllMusic</a> noted the song has "a catchy hook and endearing melody, with a reminiscent <a href="/wiki/Eurodance" title="Eurodance">euro-dance</a> rhythm."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allmusic_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>After "Sometimes" is <i>...Baby One More Time's</i> fourth track, "Soda Pop", a song that draws influences from <a href="/wiki/Bubblegum_pop" title="Bubblegum pop">bubblegum pop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dancehall" title="Dancehall">dancehall</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allmusic_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-amazon1_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-amazon1-21">[21]</a></sup> and features background vocals from co-writer Mikey Bassie.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-liner_5-3"><a href="#cite_note-liner-5">[5]</a></sup> Spears' vocals on the fifth track and fourth single, "<a href="/wiki/Born_to_Make_You_Happy" title="Born to Make You Happy">Born to Make You Happy</a>", span more than an <a href="/wiki/Octave" title="Octave">octave</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> Its lyrics allude to a relationship that a woman desires to repair, not quite understanding what went wrong, as she comes to realize that "I don't know how to live without your love/I was born to make you happy".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-popology_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-popology-23">[23]</a></sup> The sixth track and final single, "<a href="/wiki/From_the_Bottom_of_My_Broken_Heart" title="From the Bottom of My Broken Heart">From the Bottom of My Broken Heart</a>", is a sentimental slow-tempo <a href="/wiki/Teen_pop" title="Teen pop">teen pop</a> ballad.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> "I Will Be There" features a guitar riff similar to <a href="/wiki/Natalie_Imbruglia" title="Natalie Imbruglia">Natalie Imbruglia</a>'s "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Torn_(Natalie_Imbruglia_song)" title="Torn (Natalie Imbruglia song)">Torn</a>" (1997), with a "rousing chorus about standing by your man (or a best friend or a house pet)", as noted by Kyle Anderson of <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a>. The eleventh track, "E-Mail My Heart", is a sensitive piano ballad where Spears sings, "E-mail me back/ And say our love will stay alive".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-popology_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-popology-23">[23]</a></sup> The cover of <a href="/wiki/Sonny_%26_Cher" title="Sonny &amp; Cher">Sonny &amp; Cher</a>'s 1967 single "<a href="/wiki/The_Beat_Goes_On_(Sonny_%26_Cher_song)" title="The Beat Goes On (Sonny &amp; Cher song)">The Beat Goes On</a>" is influenced by <a href="/wiki/Bossa_nova" title="Bossa nova">bossa nova</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trip_hop" title="Trip hop">trip hop</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-popology_23-2"><a href="#cite_note-popology-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-toronto_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-toronto-27">[27]</a></sup> and features a similar sound to <a href="/wiki/Spy_film" title="Spy film">spy movies</a> themes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-popology_23-3"><a href="#cite_note-popology-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_reception">Critical reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=...Baby_One_More_Time_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Critical reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<td style="text-align:center;vertical-align:middle"><i><a href="/wiki/The_Hamilton_Spectator" title="The Hamilton Spectator">The Hamilton Spectator</a></i></td>
<td style="text-align:center;vertical-align:middle"><span style="white-space:nowrap" title="2.5/5 stars"><img alt="2.5/5 stars" data-file-height="110" data-file-width="108" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/11px-Star_full.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/17px-Star_full.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/22px-Star_full.svg.png 2x" title="2.5/5 stars" width="11"/><img alt="" data-file-height="110" data-file-width="108" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/11px-Star_full.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/17px-Star_full.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/22px-Star_full.svg.png 2x" width="11"/><img alt="" data-file-height="110" data-file-width="108" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Star_half.svg/11px-Star_half.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Star_half.svg/17px-Star_half.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Star_half.svg/22px-Star_half.svg.png 2x" width="11"/><img alt="" data-file-height="110" data-file-width="108" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Star_empty.svg/11px-Star_empty.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Star_empty.svg/17px-Star_empty.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Star_empty.svg/22px-Star_empty.svg.png 2x" width="11"/><img alt="" data-file-height="110" data-file-width="108" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Star_empty.svg/11px-Star_empty.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Star_empty.svg/17px-Star_empty.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Star_empty.svg/22px-Star_empty.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></span><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hamilton_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-hamilton-34">[34]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><i>...Baby One More Time</i> received mixed reviews from critics. Stephen Thomas Erlewine of Allmusic gave the album four out of five stars,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-erlewine1999_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-erlewine1999-35">[35]</a></sup> and commented that, by the time Spears launched her career, "everything old was new again", comparing the album to <i><a href="/wiki/Hangin%27_Tough" title="Hangin' Tough">Hangin' Tough</a></i> (1988) by <a href="/wiki/New_Kids_on_the_Block" title="New Kids on the Block">New Kids on the Block</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allmusic_20-3"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-20">[20]</a></sup> Erlewine further complimented the quality of the singles while praising Max Martin, "who is also the mastermind behind Spears' debut."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allmusic_20-4"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-20">[20]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a>'</i>s Beth Johnson noted the singer "sounds remarkably like the <a href="/wiki/Backstreet_Boys" title="Backstreet Boys">Backstreet Boys</a>' kid sister", saying, however, that this was "not surprising, since BSB hit-meister Max Martin wrote the candy-pop-with-a-funky-edge smash debut."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ew_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-ew-30">[30]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Robert_Christgau" title="Robert Christgau">Robert Christgau</a> commented Spears portrayed a "Madonna next door" in the album with songs like "...Baby One More Time" and "Soda Pop",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-christgau_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-christgau-29">[29]</a></sup> while Craig McDennis of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hamilton_Spectator" title="The Hamilton Spectator">The Hamilton Spectator</a></i> said the album "offers a glib compendium of soul/pop cliches, served with a giddy, uptempo verve that recalls <a href="/wiki/Debbie_Gibson" title="Debbie Gibson">Debbie Gibson</a> on a chocolate high."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hamilton_34-1"><a href="#cite_note-hamilton-34">[34]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Amazon.com" title="Amazon.com">Amazon.com</a>'s Rickey Wright gave <i>...Baby One More Time</i> a mixed review, saying that "a few of the disc's cuts are pleasantly catchy",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-amazon1_21-2"><a href="#cite_note-amazon1-21">[21]</a></sup> noting, however, "neither does the 17-year-old Spears's debut album contain anything else that remotely approaches that instant hit single ['...Baby One More Time']."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-amazon1_21-3"><a href="#cite_note-amazon1-21">[21]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s Paul Verna considered the album "a top 40-ready workout filled with hook-laden songs from the same bag as the title cut".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spotlightbill_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-spotlightbill-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>Kyle Anderson of <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a> said he "was surprised in more ways than one "with his first listening of <i>...Baby One More Time</i>, commenting he "expected there to be a lot of filler (there sort of is), though I didn't expect it to be as odd (at least sonically) as it ended up being. There has never been any mystery to why Spears became such a superstar, but these songs probably would have been huge even if Britney wore burlap sacks in all of her videos."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-popology_23-5"><a href="#cite_note-popology-23">[23]</a></sup> Barry Walters of <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> gave the album two stars out of five,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-...Baby_One_More_Time_Album_Review_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-...Baby_One_More_Time_Album_Review-31">[31]</a></sup> and compared the album's sound to early hits of Debbie Gibson, Mariah Carey, and <a href="/wiki/Samantha_Fox" title="Samantha Fox">Samantha Fox</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-...Baby_One_More_Time_Album_Review_31-2"><a href="#cite_note-...Baby_One_More_Time_Album_Review-31">[31]</a></sup> Walters also said that "while several Cherion-crafted kiddie-funk jams serve up beefy hooks, shameless schlock slowies, like 'E-Mail My Heart', are pure spam."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-...Baby_One_More_Time_Album_Review_31-3"><a href="#cite_note-...Baby_One_More_Time_Album_Review-31">[31]</a></sup> A <i><a href="/wiki/NME" title="NME">NME</a></i> reviewer rated <i>...Baby One More Time</i> 1 out of 10, saying that "we seem to have reached crisis point: pubescent pop is now so rife that 17-year-old Britney 'lizard-lounge' Spears is already halfway through her lucrative showbiz career".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nme_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-nme-36">[36]</a></sup> He also found the album premature, commenting, "hopefully, if she starts to live the wretched life that we all eventually do, her voice will show the scars, she'll stop looking so fucking smug, she'll find solace in drugs and we'll be all the more happier for it. Now grow up, girl. Quick!"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nme_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-nme-36">[36]</a></sup> Amanda Murray of <a href="/wiki/Sputnikmusic" title="Sputnikmusic">Sputnikmusic</a> felt that, "with the exception of the terrific title track, <i>...Baby One More Time</i> is a collection of either competent pop songs underwhelmingly executed or underwhelmingly written pop songs competently executed."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sputnik_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-sputnik-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_performance">Commercial performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=...Baby_One_More_Time_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Commercial performance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Britney_Spears_2002_1.jpg"><img alt="Image of a blond female performer. She is turning her back to the camera, near the end of the stage. She is wearing black pants and a black top with long sleeves, showing her midriff. In front of her, a female dancer is climbing into a pole. A crowd of people clapping, screaming and taking pictures stands can be seen in the audience." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="375" data-file-width="500" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Britney_Spears_2002_1.jpg/220px-Britney_Spears_2002_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Britney_Spears_2002_1.jpg/330px-Britney_Spears_2002_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Britney_Spears_2002_1.jpg/440px-Britney_Spears_2002_1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Britney_Spears_2002_1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Spears performing "<a href="/wiki/(You_Drive_Me)_Crazy" title="(You Drive Me) Crazy">(You Drive Me) Crazy</a>" during the <a href="/wiki/Dream_Within_a_Dream_Tour" title="Dream Within a Dream Tour">Dream Within a Dream Tour</a>, 2001.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><i>...Baby One More Time</i> debuted at the top of the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> selling 121,000 units,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britneyfirstweekstats_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-britneyfirstweekstats-37">[37]</a></sup> replacing <a href="/wiki/DMX_(rapper)" title="DMX (rapper)">DMX</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Flesh_of_My_Flesh,_Blood_of_My_Blood" title="Flesh of My Flesh, Blood of My Blood">Flesh of My Flesh, Blood of My Blood</a></i> (1998).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britneyfirstweekstats_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-britneyfirstweekstats-37">[37]</a></sup> Spears broke several records by doing so.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-records_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-records-38">[38]</a></sup> The singer became the first new female artist to have a number one single on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 and number one album on the <i>Billboard</i> 200 at the same time;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-records_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-records-38">[38]</a></sup> the first new artist (male or female) to have a single go to the number one spot the same week that the album debuted at number one;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-records_38-2"><a href="#cite_note-records-38">[38]</a></sup> and the first new female artist to have the first single and first album at number one the same week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-records_38-3"><a href="#cite_note-records-38">[38]</a></sup> Spears is also the youngest female in <i>Billboard</i> history to have a simultaneous single and album at number one in the same week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-records_38-4"><a href="#cite_note-records-38">[38]</a></sup> After four weeks since its release, the album had sold more than 500,000 copies, according to <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_SoundScan" title="Nielsen SoundScan">Nielsen SoundScan</a> sales data.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> After dropping to the top five, the album went back to number one in its fourth week, with a total of 804,200 units sold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> On its fifth week it reached its highest sales week with 229,000 copies sold. <i>...Baby One More Time</i> spent a total of six non-consecutive weeks at number one,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britneyfirsttour_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-britneyfirsttour-41">[41]</a></sup> and sold more than 1.8 million copies in its first two months of release in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britneyfifthweek_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-britneyfifthweek-42">[42]</a></sup> In its 47th week on the <i>Billboard</i> 200, the album held strong at number three, and with sales of over of 10 million copies in the United States alone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-diamond_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-diamond-43">[43]</a></sup> The album was later certified Diamond by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-riaadiamond_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-riaadiamond-44">[44]</a></sup> making Spears the youngest artist to receive that award, breaking <a href="/wiki/Alanis_Morissette" title="Alanis Morissette">Alanis Morissette</a>'s record, who was 21 when she released <i><a href="/wiki/Jagged_Little_Pill" title="Jagged Little Pill">Jagged Little Pill</a></i> (1995).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-riaadiamond_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-riaadiamond-44">[44]</a></sup> The album was the fourteenth album since 1991 to sell over 10 million copies in the United States,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> and Spears became the best-selling female artist of 1999.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-riaadiamond_44-2"><a href="#cite_note-riaadiamond-44">[44]</a></sup> <i>...Baby One More Time</i> spent a total of fifty-one weeks in the top ten of the <i>Billboard</i> 200.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britneynewalbum_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-britneynewalbum-46">[46]</a></sup> The album spent a total of 103 weeks on the chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> <i>...Baby One More Time</i> landed at number three on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BMG" title="BMG">BMG</a> Music Club all-time best-sellers list, selling 1.6 million units, behind <a href="/wiki/Shania_Twain" title="Shania Twain">Shania Twain</a>'s <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Come_on_Over_(Shania_Twain_album)" title="Come on Over (Shania Twain album)">Come on Over</a></i> (1997).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BMG_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-BMG-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p>The album debuted at number one on the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Albums_Chart" title="Canadian Albums Chart">Canadian Albums Chart</a>, totaling nine non-consecutive weeks at the top.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> On December 12, 1999, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadian_Recording_Industry_Association" title="Canadian Recording Industry Association">Canadian Recording Industry Association</a> certified it Diamond, for sales over 1 million units.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CanadaBritney_SpearsBaby_One_More_TimealbumCertRef_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-CanadaBritney_SpearsBaby_One_More_TimealbumCertRef-52">[52]</a></sup> <i>...Baby One More Time</i> spent two weeks at number two on the <a href="/wiki/European_Top_100_Albums" title="European Top 100 Albums">European Top 100 Albums</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1990sbb_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-1990sbb-53">[53]</a></sup> and sold over four million copies within the continent, being certified quadruple Platinum by the <a href="/wiki/International_Federation_of_the_Phonographic_Industry" title="International Federation of the Phonographic Industry">International Federation of the Phonographic Industry</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EuropeBritney_SpearsBaby_One_More_TimealbumCertRef_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-EuropeBritney_SpearsBaby_One_More_TimealbumCertRef-54">[54]</a></sup> The album reached number two in the <a href="/wiki/UK_Albums_Chart" title="UK Albums Chart">United Kingdom</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK_charts_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-UK_charts-55">[55]</a></sup> number four in <a href="/wiki/Syndicat_National_de_l%27%C3%89dition_Phonographique" title="Syndicat National de l'Édition Phonographique">France</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-French_charts_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-French_charts-56">[56]</a></sup> and was certified triple Platinum by the <a href="/wiki/British_Phonographic_Industry" title="British Phonographic Industry">British Phonographic Industry</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-United_KingdomBritney_SpearsBaby_One_More_TimealbumCertRef_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-United_KingdomBritney_SpearsBaby_One_More_TimealbumCertRef-57">[57]</a></sup> double Platinum by the <a href="/wiki/Syndicat_National_de_l%27%C3%89dition_Phonographique" title="Syndicat National de l'Édition Phonographique">Syndicat National de l'Édition Phonographique</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FranceBritney_SpearsBaby_One_More_TimealbumCertRef_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-FranceBritney_SpearsBaby_One_More_TimealbumCertRef-58">[58]</a></sup> triple Gold in Germany by the <a href="/wiki/International_Federation_of_the_Phonographic_Industry" title="International Federation of the Phonographic Industry">International Federation of the Phonographic Industry</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GermanyBritney_SpearsBaby_One_More_TimealbumCertRef_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-GermanyBritney_SpearsBaby_One_More_TimealbumCertRef-59">[59]</a></sup> and ten-times Platinum (Diamond) by the <a href="/wiki/Polish_Society_of_the_Phonographic_Industry" title="Polish Society of the Phonographic Industry">Polish Society of the Phonographic Industry</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PolandBritneySpearsBaby_One_More_TimealbumCertRef_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-PolandBritneySpearsBaby_One_More_TimealbumCertRef-60">[60]</a></sup> <i>...Baby One More Time</i> debuted at number nine in May 1999 on the <a href="/wiki/ARIA_Charts" title="ARIA Charts">Australian Albums Chart</a>, reaching at number two nine weeks later, placing behind the <a href="/wiki/Dawson%27s_Creek#Music" title="Dawson's Creek"><i>Dawson's Creek</i> soundtrack</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ARIA_charts_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-ARIA_charts-61">[61]</a></sup> The album became the seventh highest-selling of 1999 in the country, and was certified four-times Platinum by the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Recording_Industry_Association" title="Australian Recording Industry Association">Australian Recording Industry Association</a> the following year after shipping 280,000 copies to retailers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AustraliaBritney_SpearsBaby_One_More_TimealbumCertRef_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-AustraliaBritney_SpearsBaby_One_More_TimealbumCertRef-63">[63]</a></sup> The track debuted at number three in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_New_Zealand" title="Recording Industry Association of New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, placing behind Shania Twain's <i>Come on Over</i> and <a href="/wiki/The_Corrs" title="The Corrs">The Corrs</a>'.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RIANZ_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-RIANZ-64">[64]</a></sup> The album was later certified triple Platinum in the country by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_New_Zealand" title="Recording Industry Association of New Zealand">Recording Industry Association of New Zealand</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-New_ZealandBritney_SpearsBaby_One_More_TimealbumCertRef_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-New_ZealandBritney_SpearsBaby_One_More_TimealbumCertRef-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Singles">Singles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=...Baby_One_More_Time_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Singles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/...Baby_One_More_Time_(song)" title="...Baby One More Time (song)">...Baby One More Time</a>" was released as Spears' debut single on October 23, 1998.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> The song received generally favorable critical reviews, mostly praising its composition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rs1_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-rs1-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allmusic_20-5"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-20">[20]</a></sup> "...Baby One More Time" attained worldwide success, reaching number one in every European country where it charted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> It received numerous certifications around the world, and is one of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_singles_worldwide" title="List of best-selling singles worldwide">best-selling singles of all time</a>, at over ten million copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> An accompanying music video, directed by <a href="/wiki/Nigel_Dick" title="Nigel Dick">Nigel Dick</a>, portrays Spears as a student from a <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic</a> high school, who starts to <a href="/wiki/Daydream" title="Daydream">daydream</a> that she is singing and dancing around the school, while watching her love interest from afar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> In 2010, the music video for "...Baby One More Time" was voted the third-most influential video in the history of <a href="/wiki/Pop_music" title="Pop music">pop music</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/Sometimes_(Britney_Spears_song)" title="Sometimes (Britney Spears song)">Sometimes</a>" was released as the second single on April 30, 1999.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britstory_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-britstory-71">[71]</a></sup> "Sometimes" achieved commercial success worldwide, reaching number one in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ultratop_50" title="Ultratop 50">Belgium (Flanders)</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mega_Single_Top_100" title="Mega Single Top 100">Netherlands</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_New_Zealand" title="Recording Industry Association of New Zealand">New Zealand</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sometimes_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-sometimes-72">[72]</a></sup> while peaking inside the top five in four countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sometimes_72-1"><a href="#cite_note-sometimes-72">[72]</a></sup> In the United States, "Sometimes" missed the top ten, peaking at number twenty-one on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> The music video for the song was directed by Nigel Dick.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trl_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-trl-74">[74]</a></sup> During rehearsals, on February 11, 1999, Spears injured her left knee and needed surgery.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-injuree_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-injuree-75">[75]</a></sup> After recuperating in <a href="/wiki/Kentwood,_Louisiana" title="Kentwood, Louisiana">Kentwood, Louisiana</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-injuree_75-1"><a href="#cite_note-injuree-75">[75]</a></sup> the music video was shot on April 9–10, 1999 at Paradise Cove in <a href="/wiki/Malibu,_California" title="Malibu, California">Malibu, California</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> It was released on May 6, 1999, on <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Total_Request_Live" title="Total Request Live">Total Request Live</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trl_74-1"><a href="#cite_note-trl-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<p>In May 1999, Max Martin and Spears went to the Battery Studios in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_City,_New_York" title="New York City, New York">New York City, New York</a>, to re-record the vocals of "<a href="/wiki/(You_Drive_Me)_Crazy" title="(You Drive Me) Crazy">(You Drive Me) Crazy</a>",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> due to the fact that a remixed version called "The Stop! Remix" was going to be included on the original motion picture soundtrack of the film <i><a href="/wiki/Drive_Me_Crazy" title="Drive Me Crazy">Drive Me Crazy</a></i> (1999).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> "The Stop! Remix" of the song was released as the third single on August 23, 1999.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britstory_71-1"><a href="#cite_note-britstory-71">[71]</a></sup> The Stop! Remix had the addition of a stanza where Spears yells "Stop!", then all sound cutting out, followed by a transition. It also omits the lines "Lovin' You Means So Much More, More than anything I ever Loved Before".</p>
<p>The music video was directed by Nigel Dick, and featured actors <a href="/wiki/Melissa_Joan_Hart" title="Melissa Joan Hart">Melissa Joan Hart</a> and <a href="/wiki/Adrian_Grenier" title="Adrian Grenier">Adrian Grenier</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/Born_to_Make_You_Happy" title="Born to Make You Happy">Born to Make You Happy</a>" was released on December 6, 1999, as the fourth single,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-swedenbtmyh_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-swedenbtmyh-80">[80]</a></sup> and received mixed reviews from music critics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-popology_23-6"><a href="#cite_note-popology-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> The song achieved commercial success, peaking inside the top-five in eleven countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-swedenbtmyh_80-1"><a href="#cite_note-swedenbtmyh-80">[80]</a></sup> The music video for it was directed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Billie_Woodruff" title="Billie Woodruff">Billie Woodruff</a> and produced by Geneva Films,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> choreographed by <a href="/wiki/Wade_Robson" title="Wade Robson">Wade Robson</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/From_the_Bottom_of_My_Broken_Heart" title="From the Bottom of My Broken Heart">From the Bottom of My Broken Heart</a>" was released on December 15, 1999, as the final single.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> The song also received mixed reviews, finding the song a classic hit and competent single, despite considering it as an unremarkable song that refers only to kissing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-popology_23-7"><a href="#cite_note-popology-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sputnik_33-2"><a href="#cite_note-sputnik-33">[33]</a></sup> "From the Bottom of My Broken Heart" achieved moderate success, peaking at number thirty-seven in Australia, and twenty-three in New Zealand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> Through imports, the song reached one hundred seventy-four in the United Kingdom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zobbel_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-zobbel-86">[86]</a></sup> In the United States, "From the Bottom of My Broken Heart" reached number fourteen on <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100, and seventeen on Pop Songs,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> and was later certified Platinum by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> (RIAA) on March 28, 2000, for selling over 1,000,000 physical units of the single.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> The music video, directed by <a href="/wiki/Gregory_Dark" title="Gregory Dark">Gregory Dark</a>, was released on December 17, 1999.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newtour_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-newtour-89">[89]</a></sup> It was highly criticized due to the fact that Dark had previously directed porn films.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Promotion">Promotion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=...Baby_One_More_Time_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Promotion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Britney_Spears_Live_Paris_6.jpg"><img alt="A blond female performer. She is standing on a moving jungle gym, wearing black and white clothes." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2189" data-file-width="3011" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Britney_Spears_Live_Paris_6.jpg/220px-Britney_Spears_Live_Paris_6.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Britney_Spears_Live_Paris_6.jpg/330px-Britney_Spears_Live_Paris_6.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Britney_Spears_Live_Paris_6.jpg/440px-Britney_Spears_Live_Paris_6.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Britney_Spears_Live_Paris_6.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Spears performing "<a href="/wiki/...Baby_One_More_Time_(song)" title="...Baby One More Time (song)">...Baby One More Time</a>" during <a href="/wiki/The_Circus_Starring_Britney_Spears" title="The Circus Starring Britney Spears">The Circus Starring Britney Spears</a>, 2009.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Promotion began in 1998, when Spears did a small tour in malls and food courts that were located mostly in larger cities around the United States and Canada. Each show lasted around 30 minutes, and Spears had two male dancers with her on the stage. The promo tour is also known as the L'Oreal Mall Tour, after its sponsor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blandford28_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-blandford28-11">[11]</a></sup> The singer made several promotional appearances including talk shows and live performances around the world. On December 1998, Spears' first showed up on MTV's and the Box's most-requested video charts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britneyfirstperformances_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-britneyfirstperformances-92">[92]</a></sup> She also appeared on the <i><a href="/wiki/Ricki_Lake_(TV_series)" title="Ricki Lake (TV series)">Ricki Lake Show</a></i>, the <i>Howie Mandel Show</i>, and was the presenter of the 1999 <a href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards_of_1999" title="American Music Awards of 1999">American Music Awards</a>, prior to the release of the album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britneyfirstperformances_92-1"><a href="#cite_note-britneyfirstperformances-92">[92]</a></sup> The singer also appeared on MTV's <i>Spring Break</i> and on the 100th episode of <a href="/wiki/Nickelodeon" title="Nickelodeon">Nickelodeon</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/All_That" title="All That">All That</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sidelined_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-sidelined-93">[93]</a></sup> However, after hurting her knee, she had rescheduled appearances several shows such as <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tonight_Show_with_Jay_Leno" title="The Tonight Show with Jay Leno">The Tonight Show with Jay Leno</a></i> and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Live_with_Regis_and_Kelly" title="Live with Regis and Kelly">Live With Regis And Kathie Lee</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sidelined_93-1"><a href="#cite_note-sidelined-93">[93]</a></sup> After recovering, Spears embarked on another promotional schedule. The singer appeared on Nickelodeon's 12th Annual Kids Choice Awards on May 1, MTV's <i>FANatic</i> on May 12, <i>Live With Regis &amp; Kathie Lee</i> on May 3, and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Rosie_O%27Donnell_Show" title="The Rosie O'Donnell Show">The Rosie O'Donnell Show</a></i> on May 25.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britneyfirsttour_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-britneyfirsttour-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>Outside the United States, Spears visited German talk show <i><a href="/wiki/Wetten,_dass..%3F" title="Wetten, dass..?">Wetten, dass..?</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Top_of_the_Pops" title="Top of the Pops">Top of the Pops</a></i> on June 25, 1999.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britneylateperformances_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-britneylateperformances-94">[94]</a></sup> She also went to the United Kingdom, making appearances on programmes such as <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/This_Morning_(TV_series)" title="This Morning (TV series)">This Morning</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/CD:UK" title="CD:UK">CD:UK</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/National_Lottery_(United_Kingdom)" title="National Lottery (United Kingdom)">National Lottery</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britneylateperformances_94-1"><a href="#cite_note-britneylateperformances-94">[94]</a></sup> She visited a music variety show called <i><a href="/wiki/Hey!_Hey!_Hey!_Music_Champ" title="Hey! Hey! Hey! Music Champ">Hey! Hey! Hey! Music Champ</a></i> in Japan, and performed at the Festival Bar in Italy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britneylateperformances_94-2"><a href="#cite_note-britneylateperformances-94">[94]</a></sup> Spears was also featured on an episode of <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">ABC</a> television sitcom, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sabrina,_The_Teenage_Witch" title="Sabrina, The Teenage Witch">Sabrina, The Teenage Witch</a></i>, where she played herself.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britneylateperformances_94-3"><a href="#cite_note-britneylateperformances-94">[94]</a></sup> Spears was returning a favor to actress <a href="/wiki/Melissa_Joan_Hart" title="Melissa Joan Hart">Melissa Joan Hart</a>, who played a cameo role in Spears' video for "(You Drive Me) Crazy," according to <i>People</i> magazine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britneylateperformances_94-4"><a href="#cite_note-britneylateperformances-94">[94]</a></sup> The episode aired on September 24, 1999.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britneylateperformances_94-5"><a href="#cite_note-britneylateperformances-94">[94]</a></sup> The same month, Spears performed on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Rosie_O%27Donnell_Show" title="The Rosie O'Donnell Show">The Rosie O'Donnell Show</a></i> on September 27, and visited <a href="/wiki/Carson_Daly" title="Carson Daly">Carson Daly</a> on MTV's <i><a href="/wiki/Total_Request_Live" title="Total Request Live">Total Request Live</a></i> the following day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> She had a mini-<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disney" title="Disney">Disney</a> concert titled "Britney Spears &amp; Joey McIntyre In Concert." Spears and <a href="/wiki/Joey_McIntyre" title="Joey McIntyre">Joey McIntyre</a> performed live in the taped concert event.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> Promotion for the album continued in early 2000, where Spears performed at the <a href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards_of_2000" title="American Music Awards of 2000">American Music Awards of 2000</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britneynewalbum_46-1"><a href="#cite_note-britneynewalbum-46">[46]</a></sup> and also performed "From the Bottom of My Broken Heart" in a medley with "...Baby One More Time" at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2000_Grammy_Awards" title="2000 Grammy Awards">2000 Grammy Awards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britneynewalbum_46-2"><a href="#cite_note-britneynewalbum-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Touring">Touring</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=...Baby_One_More_Time_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Touring">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/...Baby_One_More_Time_Tour" title="...Baby One More Time Tour">...Baby One More Time Tour</a> and <a href="/wiki/(You_Drive_Me)_Crazy_Tour" title="(You Drive Me) Crazy Tour">(You Drive Me) Crazy Tour</a></div>
<p>On March 5, 1999, it was reported that Spears was planning her first headlining tour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-headlining_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-headlining-97">[97]</a></sup> She announced that the tour would start in July.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tuesday_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-tuesday-98">[98]</a></sup> On May 12, <a href="/wiki/Tommy_Hilfiger" title="Tommy Hilfiger">Tommy Hilfiger</a> was announced as the main tour sponsor. During the time of the announcement, Spears was being featured in the company's "AllStars" campaign.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tommy_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-tommy-99">[99]</a></sup> On December 17, during the premiere of the music video of "<a href="/wiki/From_the_Bottom_of_My_Broken_Heart" title="From the Bottom of My Broken Heart">From the Bottom of My Broken Heart</a>" on <i><a href="/wiki/Total_Request_Live" title="Total Request Live">TRL</a></i>, Spears called the show to announce March 2000 US tour dates. The extension, entitled Crazy 2K Tour, was considered a prelude to her <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oops!..._I_Did_It_Again_World_Tour" title="Oops!... I Did It Again World Tour">future world tour</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newtour_89-1"><a href="#cite_note-newtour-89">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rolling_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-rolling-100">[100]</a></sup> The leg's main sponsor was <a href="/wiki/Got_Milk%3F" title="Got Milk?">Got Milk?</a>. Media director Peter Gardiner explained, "Britney is magic with teen-age girls, and that's an absolutely crucial target for milk". Spears shot an advertising campaign to be shown before her performances began.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-milk_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-milk-101">[101]</a></sup> The secondary sponsor was <a href="/wiki/Polaroid_Corporation" title="Polaroid Corporation">Polaroid</a> and the corporation released the <a href="/wiki/I-Zone" title="I-Zone">Polaroid I-Zone</a> as the tour's official camera. Spears used the I-Zone onstage to take pictures of the audience and further promote the product.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-polaroid_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-polaroid-102">[102]</a></sup> The show was divided into segments, separated by interlude, ending with an encore.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sfc_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-sfc-103">[103]</a></sup> The setlist consisted of songs from her debut album and several <a href="/wiki/Cover_version" title="Cover version">covers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sfc_103-1"><a href="#cite_note-sfc-103">[103]</a></sup> Some changes were made during the 2000 leg, with the covers replaced by songs from her second studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Oops!..._I_Did_It_Again_(album)" title="Oops!... I Did It Again (album)">Oops!... I Did It Again</a></i>. The tour received positive critical appreciation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usatoday_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-usatoday-104">[104]</a></sup> During the tour, Spears was accused of lip synching, although she denied these claims.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rolling_100-1"><a href="#cite_note-rolling-100">[100]</a></sup> On April 20, 2000, the concert at <a href="/wiki/Hilton_Hawaiian_Village" title="Hilton Hawaiian Village">Hilton Hawaiian Village</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Honolulu,_Hawaii" title="Honolulu, Hawaii">Honolulu, Hawaii</a>, was taped.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tusca_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-tusca-105">[105]</a></sup> It was slightly altered from its Crazy 2K incarnation and featured different costumes. On June 5, 2000, it was broadcast on <a href="/wiki/Fox_Broadcasting_Company" title="Fox Broadcasting Company">Fox</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fox_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-fox-106">[106]</a></sup> The special was aired several times during the year. On November 21, 2000, JIVE Records released the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Live_and_More!" title="Live and More!">Live and More!</a></i> <a href="/wiki/DVD" title="DVD">DVD</a>, which included the Fox special.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-herald_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-herald-107">[107]</a></sup> It was certified triple Platinum by the RIAA for shipping 300,000 units.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=...Baby_One_More_Time_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: left; clear: left; margin: 0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0; width:30%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"With <i>...Baby One More Time</i>, I didn't get to show my voice off. The songs were great, but they weren't very challenging."</p>
</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: left;">—Spears reflects on <i>...Baby One More Time</i> in December 1999.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></cite></div>
<p>Spears was credited with leading the revival of <a href="/wiki/Teen_pop" title="Teen pop">teen pop</a>. <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Daily_Yomiuri" title="The Daily Yomiuri">The Daily Yomiuri</a></i> reported that "critics have hailed her as the most gifted teenage pop idol for many years, but Spears has set her sights a little higher-she is aiming for the level of superstardom that has been achieved by Madonna and Janet Jackson."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> <i>Rolling Stone</i> wrote: "Britney Spears carries on the classic archetype of the rock &amp; roll teen queen, the dungaree doll, the angel baby who just has to make a scene."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> Rami Yacoub who co-produced Spears's debut album with lyricist Max Martin commented, "I know from Denniz Pop and Max's previous productions, when we do songs, there's kind of a nasal thing. With N' Sync and the Backstreet Boys, we had to push for that mid-nasal voice. When Britney did that, she got this kind of raspy, sexy voice."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard_book_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-billboard_book-112">[112]</a></sup> Chuck Taylor of <i>Billboard</i> observed, "Spears has become a consummate performer, with snappy dance moves, a clearly real-albeit young-and funkdified voice ... "(You Drive Me) Crazy", her third single ... demonstrates Spears' own development, proving that the 17-year-old is finding her own vocal personality after so many months of steadfast practice."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> Stephen Thomas Erlewine of Allmusic referred to her music as a "blend of infectious, rap-inflected dance-pop and smooth balladry."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allmusic_20-6"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-20">[20]</a></sup> Sputnikmusic writer Amanda Murray noted the album "offers a marker for Spears' progression as an artist, as a celebrity, and as a woman."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sputnik_33-3"><a href="#cite_note-sputnik-33">[33]</a></sup> In 2010, the album was included in the book <i><a href="/wiki/1001_Albums_You_Must_Hear_Before_You_Die" title="1001 Albums You Must Hear Before You Die">1001 Albums You Must Hear Before You Die</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
<p>Spears became an international <a href="/wiki/Pop_icon" title="Pop icon">pop culture icon</a> immediately after launching her recording career. <i>Rolling Stone</i> magazine wrote: "One of the most controversial and successful female vocalists of the 21st century," she "spearheaded the rise of post-millennial teen pop ... Spears early on cultivated a mixture of innocence and experience that broke the bank".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> She is listed by the <i><a href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Records" title="Guinness World Records">Guinness World Records</a></i> as having the "Best-selling album by a teenage solo artist".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> Melissa Ruggieri of the <i><a href="/wiki/Richmond_Times-Dispatch" title="Richmond Times-Dispatch">Richmond Times-Dispatch</a></i> reported, "She's also marked for being the best-selling teenage artist. Before she turned 20 in 2001, Spears sold more than 30 million albums worldwide".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> Barbara Ellen of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Observer" title="The Observer">The Observer</a></i> has reported: "Spears is famously one of the 'oldest' teenagers pop has ever produced, almost middle aged in terms of focus and determination. Many 19-year-olds haven't even started working by that age, whereas Britney, a former Mouseketeer, was that most unusual and volatile of American phenomena — a child with a full-time career. While other little girls were putting posters on their walls, Britney was wanting to be the poster on the wall. Whereas other children develop at their own pace, Britney was developing at a pace set by the ferociously competitive American entertainment industry".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> <i>...Baby One More Time</i> is Spears' most successful album to date, with worldwide sales over 30 million copies,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> and also the best-selling album by a teenage solo artist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup></p>

<td style="padding-right:10px;text-align:right;vertical-align:top">4.</td>
<td style="vertical-align:top">"...Baby One More Time" <span style="font-size:85%">(Answering Machine Message)</span></td>
<td style="vertical-align:top"> </td>
<td style="vertical-align:top"> </td>
<td style="padding-right:10px;text-align:right;vertical-align:top"><span class="duration"><span class="min">0</span>:<span class="s">21</span></span></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="4" style="padding:0"><span style="width:7.5em;float:right;padding-left:10px;background-color:#eee;margin-right:2px"><b>Total length:</b></span></td>
<td style="padding:0 10px 0 0;text-align:right;background-color:#eee"><b><span class="duration"><span class="min">11</span>:<span class="s">27</span></span></b></td>
</tr>
</table>
<dl>
<dt>Notes</dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li>In North America the album was issued as an Enhanced CD which allowed access to bonus videos, photos and more when inserted into a computer.</li>
<li>The very first pressings of the album feature a hidden spoken message by Spears after "The Beat Goes On". In it, Spears thanks fans and promotes the then-upcoming <a href="/wiki/Backstreet_Boys" title="Backstreet Boys">Backstreet Boys</a> album, <i><a href="/wiki/Millennium_(Backstreet_Boys_album)" title="Millennium (Backstreet Boys album)">Millennium</a></i>, with snippets of songs featured on the album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-popology_23-8"><a href="#cite_note-popology-23">[23]</a></sup></li>
<li><sup><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_a"><b><a href="#ref_a">^a</a></b></span></sup> signifies a co-<a href="/wiki/Record_producer" title="Record producer">producer</a></li>
<li><sup><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_b"><b><a href="#ref_b">^b</a></b></span></sup> signifies an additional <a href="/wiki/Record_producer" title="Record producer">producer</a></li>
<li><sup><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_c"><b><a href="#ref_c">^c</a></b></span></sup> signifies a <a href="/wiki/Remix" title="Remix">remixer</a></li>
</ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=...Baby_One_More_Time_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-167"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-167">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">As of March 2015, <i>...Baby One More Time</i> has sold 10,600,000 copies in the US according to <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_SoundScan" title="Nielsen SoundScan">Nielsen SoundScan</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard2015_165-0"><a href="#cite_note-billboard2015-165">[165]</a></sup> with additional 1,600,000 sold at BMG Music Clubs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BMG_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-BMG-48">[48]</a></sup> Nielsen SoundScan does not count albums sold through clubs like the BMG Music Service, which were significantly popular in the 1990s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ask_Billboard_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ask_Billboard-166">[166]</a></sup></span></li>
</ol>
</div>
